    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_35ceef0a-05e3-476a-af34-b77d0ef15b13'

  <span id="freeText4242469160637648697" style="display:none">What begins as the story of a lost boy turns into a story of a brave man yearning to understand what happened that night, in the years since, and to his very person.<br /><br />While on vacation with their parents, Matthew Homes and his older brother snuck out in the middle of the night. Only Matthew came home safely. Ten years later, Matthew tells us, he has found a way to bring his brother back... <br /><br />What begins as the story of a lost boy turns into a story of a brave man yearning to understand what happened that night, in the years since, and to his very person. Unafraid to look at the shadows of our hearts, Nathan Filer's rare and brilliant debut shows us the strength that is rooted in resilience and love. <br /><br />Editor's Note Feb 10, 2014: St Martin's Press have just announced that Where The Moon Isn't will be republished under the UK title, The Shock and The Fall this week in digital format and later this fall in paperback. They said that the title change was necessary "because otherwise there's a lot of confusion" - The Shock and The Fall recently won the Costa Book of the Year award, which is UK based but has international renown.</span>

This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    Did anyone actually read the book?! Yes, Simon is ill, and carrying Matthew after Matthew falls down doesn't do his health any good. However, it's act<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    Did anyone actually read the book?! Yes, Simon is ill, and carrying Matthew after Matthew falls down doesn't do his health any good. However, it's actually a few days later that Simon dies, by falling himself at the same location that Matthew did. Unfortunately he's not as lucky as Matthew; and therefore Matthews feels guilt because he was unable to save his brother.<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>
  
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>

<div id="review_827063775" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/827063775" />
    <a title="Paul Bryant" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/416390-paul-bryant"><img alt="Paul Bryant" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1224113172p2/416390.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/827063775?book_show_action=true">Jan 18, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paul Bryant" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paul Bryant" href="/user/show/416390-paul-bryant">Paul Bryant</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/416390-paul-bryant?shelf=novels">novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/416390-paul-bryant?shelf=mentalillness">mentalillness</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer827063775" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7525472603942534183">Another novel to prove, if proof was needed, how utterly heartless and without pity I am becoming. Sorry, Nathan Filer, I come to rain all over your parade. Well, quite a lot of it.<br/><br/>The blurb has these three little sentences:<br/><br/><i>There are books you can’t stop reading, which keep you up all night</i><br/><br/>(Well, I actually was reading this most of last night, but that’s because I had insomnia.)<br/><br/><i>There are books which let us into the hidden parts of life and make them vividly real. </i><br/><br/>(Referring to the world of the s</span>
  <span id="freeText7525472603942534183" style="display:none">Another novel to prove, if proof was needed, how utterly heartless and without pity I am becoming. Sorry, Nathan Filer, I come to rain all over your parade. Well, quite a lot of it.<br /><br />The blurb has these three little sentences:<br /><br /><i>There are books you can’t stop reading, which keep you up all night</i><br /><br />(Well, I actually was reading this most of last night, but that’s because I had insomnia.)<br /><br /><i>There are books which let us into the hidden parts of life and make them vividly real. </i><br /><br />(Referring to the world of the schizophrenic, since that’s what this novel is all about. But I wouldn’t call mentally ill young people and their lives in and out of institutions a hidden part of life , there are movies (<i>Broken, Silver Linings Playbook,</i> etc etc) and books (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8526623-henry-s-demons" rel="nofollow noopener"> <i>Henry’s Demons</i></a> – recommended - and lots of others), it’s not terra incognita.<br /><br /><i>There are books which, because of the sheer skill with which every word is chosen, linger in your mind for days.</i><br /><br />(Wow, fire that blurb writer! For days you say?! Sheer skill? I suppose with not so much skill a book will only linger for minutes. So yeah, they still crank out this silly OTT hypegloop.)<br /><br /><b>THE BIG BLACK PLOT DEVICE</b><br /><br />This book won the Costa first novel award, so what do I know. I was almost completely unthrilled. It was tiresome. I mean to say, there’s this big thing which is hinted at in the first few pages and which hangs over the rest of novel like a Big Black Cloud About to Burst Forth With Torrential Rain. The schizophrenic brother whose impressionistic memoir/confession we are reading has in some way caused the death of his Down Syndrome brother (yes, this is a blighted family). Cornily, the Big Reveal of What Really Happened That Fateful Day is coughed up only on page 247. The fake suspense of waiting to find out what you figure out roughly from page 5 does not kill you. It just makes you think oh are they still using this plot device? They should really stop. <br /><br />I thought I would only write a three line bah-humbug review, but the sheer skill with which every single word was chosen has made the crabbiness I felt linger in my mind for… hours. <br /><br /><b>I’D LIKE TO TEACH THE WORLD TO SING IN PERFECT HARMONY (BUT I DON’T THINK I’LL GET ROUND TO IT)</b><br /><br />It says here -<br /><br /><i>The comedian Jo Brand has called The Shock of the Fall "one of the best books about mental illness" and judges for the Costa book awards said it was a novel "so good it will make you feel a better person".</i><br /><br />Maybe it is, maybe it will. But I thought the bleak realism and painful memories of Matt’s story did not then mean it was okay to ladle dollops of sentimental goop into the mix. It’s strange how wildly different reactions to novels can be – look at the love-gush that puthered all over Donna Tartt’s latest whopper, and look at <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/761004649" rel="nofollow noopener"> this rather good review here. </a><br /><br /><b>SOMETHING I DID LIKE</b><br /><br />You do get a very strong sense of the mental bind that some patients (or : “service users”!) get into once they’re sucked into the mental health biz. The regime is almost designed to engender fear and distrust. They’re confined to a facility. And drugs are administered to them, all of which have horrible side effects (even the drugs they give you to combat the side effects of the first drugs). And there’s no choice in any of this. They have proved they’re incapable of existing in the outside world in one way or another, so there they are, here’s their diagnosis, there’s the drugs (if you don’t take those 6 pills we’ll inject you) and there’s your room. So, the patients become locked into a low-level interior guerrilla war against the people who are trying to help them. Inside their heads – as well as fighting their illness - every mental patient is either consciously or unconsciously Jack Nicholson in <i>One Flew Over The Cuckoo’s Nest. </i> The staff are their enemies (even the nice ones). (Matt : <i>I don’t hate these people. I just hate not having the choice to get rid of them.</i>) The terminology is dehumanising. Their lives are deserts of idle hours spent smoking with a guy who talks to his tattoos. Or daytime tv, your choice. <br /><br /><i>Last time I went into the office to borrow the Nursing Dictionary, I counted three mugs, a mouse mat, a bunch of pens, two Post-It note booklets and the wall clock – all sporting the brands of different medicines. It's like being in prison and having to look at adverts for fucking locks.</i><br /><br /><b>SOMETHING ELSE I LIKED </b><br /><br />Matt is haunted by his dead brother<br /><br /><i>If the tap choked and spluttered before the water came, he was saying I’m lonely. When I opened a bottle of Dr Pepper and the caramel bubbles fizzed over the rim, he was asking me to come out and play. He could speak through an itch, the certainty of a sneeze, the after-taste of tablets, or the way sugar fell from a spoon.</i><br /><br />No doubt at all, this book has its heart in the right place, unlike mine, which was abandoned a long time ago in a left luggage locker in a train station in a town whose name I no longer recall. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7525472603942534183" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2176941001" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2176941001" />
    <a title="Charlotte May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14002983-charlotte-may"><img alt="Charlotte May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596906925p2/14002983.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2176941001?book_show_action=true">Nov 07, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Charlotte May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Charlotte May" href="/user/show/14002983-charlotte-may">Charlotte May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007491452" href="/book/show/20754586-the-shock-of-the-fall">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14002983-charlotte-may?shelf=tear-jerker">tear-jerker</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14002983-charlotte-may?shelf=contemporary-recent">contemporary-recent</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14002983-charlotte-may?shelf=illness-mental-terminal">illness-mental-terminal</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2176941001" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7493041457776670913"><i> "This is my life. I'm nineteen years old, and the only thing I have any control over in my entire world is the way I choose to tell this story. So I'm hardly going to fuck about. It would be nice if you'd try to trust me." </i><br/><br/>I am so fascinated by books that depict mental illnesses. Books such as <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/774308.The_Bell_Jar' title='The Bell Jar by Sylvia Plath' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Bell Jar</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/35900387.Eleanor_Oliphant_Is_Completely_Fine' title='Eleanor Oliphant Is Completely Fine by Gail Honeyman' rel='nofollow noopener'>Eleanor Oliphant Is Completely Fine</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34299826.Countless' title='Countless by Karen Gregory' rel='nofollow noopener'>Countless</a> just to name a few, have really touched me. The focus on the frailty of the human mind is something that resonates really strongly with me, </span>
  <span id="freeText7493041457776670913" style="display:none"><i> "This is my life. I'm nineteen years old, and the only thing I have any control over in my entire world is the way I choose to tell this story. So I'm hardly going to fuck about. It would be nice if you'd try to trust me." </i><br /><br />I am so fascinated by books that depict mental illnesses. Books such as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/774308.The_Bell_Jar" title="The Bell Jar by Sylvia Plath" rel="nofollow noopener">The Bell Jar</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/35900387.Eleanor_Oliphant_Is_Completely_Fine" title="Eleanor Oliphant Is Completely Fine by Gail Honeyman" rel="nofollow noopener">Eleanor Oliphant Is Completely Fine</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34299826.Countless" title="Countless by Karen Gregory" rel="nofollow noopener">Countless</a> just to name a few, have really touched me. The focus on the frailty of the human mind is something that resonates really strongly with me, and telling these stories is vital. Certainly for me, they remind me that none of us are alone in our suffering. <br /><br />The Shock of the Fall follows Matt, and his deteriorating mental health after the death of his brother Simon. We don't find out straight away how Simon died, and Matthew's story is not told chronologically, so at times you have to try and remember where you are. It moves from his childhood with his parents including a mother who was also mentally unwell, to his time living by himself in his flat and finally to the time he spends in a mental hospital. <br /><br /><i> "If people think you're MAD, then everything you think, will have MAD stamped across it." </i><br /><br />A lot of the story is based in my hometown of Bristol, UK, which I didn't realise at the time of picking this book, so that was a nice surprise. This book was so well written, with several parts repeated to indicate the breakdown within Matt's mind. I know very little about schizophrenia, so to read a book focusing on a character's suffering with this illness was enlightening and frightening all at once. <br /><br /><i> "We don't choose what we keep...not ever, really." </i><br /><br />Highly recommend.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7493041457776670913" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1594171533" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1594171533" />
    <a title="Petra-X" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1237196-petra-x"><img alt="Petra-X" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603179398p2/1237196.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1594171533?book_show_action=true">Mar 29, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Petra-X" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Petra-X" href="/user/show/1237196-petra-x">Petra-X</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1237196-petra-x?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1237196-petra-x?shelf=2016-150-reviews">2016-150-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1237196-petra-x?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1237196-petra-x?shelf=2016-read">2016-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1594171533" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11810930839540674628">I always find it hard to write reviews about meh books. Books I love, books I hate, I have strong feelings towards them, but meh... What do you say? <br/><br/>The book is supposedly revelations of how it really is to be schizophrenic and what life in a mental institution is really like and the author is a mental nurse so he knows. As the book has won many awards I was expecting the writing to be better than competent. Perhaps I was expecting too much having just read the searingly brilliant Man Booker pri</span>
  <span id="freeText11810930839540674628" style="display:none">I always find it hard to write reviews about meh books. Books I love, books I hate, I have strong feelings towards them, but meh... What do you say? <br /><br />The book is supposedly revelations of how it really is to be schizophrenic and what life in a mental institution is really like and the author is a mental nurse so he knows. As the book has won many awards I was expecting the writing to be better than competent. Perhaps I was expecting too much having just read the searingly brilliant Man Booker prize-winning <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20893314.A_Brief_History_of_Seven_Killings" title="A Brief History of Seven Killings by Marlon James" rel="nofollow noopener">A Brief History of Seven Killings</a>. <br /><br />I must have missed something. I didn't see Matthew's insanity at all. True, his dead brother was his constant companion, although it isn't until the last part of the book referred to that much. True he acts oddly on occasion. But only on occasion, most of the time he seems to be a rather boring young man with nothing much to say, except about himself (a point he himself makes). His thoughts don't seem particularly disordered. Nothing he says or does seems to lead one to think he is terribly ill and needs to be locked up in a secure unit and medicated with endless pills and injections. <br /><br />I've known a few schizophrenics, two very well, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/216938395" rel="nofollow noopener">one</a> before he was treated and he was mad (but lovely, I loved him) and the other after he was medicated (he was still very disordered indeed but able to go to college). I also grew up knowing several. Adding to that the books, especially in the last year or so I've read on schizophrenia, they all share one thing in common - a frame of reference when they are psychotic that has an internal logic, but is unique to them and always problematic given that it is quite different from how the world works. I didn't see this in the book at all.<br /><br />As far as how it really is in mental institutions, how the staff really are, there were no revelations. It was exactly like in tv show. Most of the patients have little to do, just medication to take, are herded from the tv room to therapy to crafts, and all of them chain-smoking. A few of the patients' behaviour is so peculiar that most of the other patients who are "ill" think that they are crazy.<br /><br />I just don't know what was supposed to be so brilliant about this book. So 2 stars meh, it was all right. And that's the best I can say about it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11810930839540674628" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1453560561" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1453560561" />
    <a title="Aj the Ravenous Reader" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader"><img alt="Aj the Ravenous Reader" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557800982p2/30248594.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1453560561?book_show_action=true">Nov 27, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aj the Ravenous Reader" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aj the Ravenous Reader" href="/user/show/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader">Aj the Ravenous Reader</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Aj the Ravenous Reader by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/17065991-ikram">Ikram</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1453560561" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10751252605960657900"><br/>I read this for Kimi's birthday tomorrow, Nov. 29! I'm posting it now because I might be too busy tomorrow. <b>HAPPY, HAPPY BIRTHDAY, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/17065991-kimi' rel='nofollow noopener'>KIMI!</a> PUT A SMILE AS BIG AS YOUR HEART BECAUSE YOU DESERVE TO BE THE HAPPIEST ON YOUR SPECIAL DAY!</b> <3 You can read her awesome review <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1007436230?book_show_action=false&from_review_page=1' rel='nofollow noopener'>here</a>.<br/><br/><b> Review </b><br/><br/>This is an interesting read that deals with mental illness, more particularly schizophrenia as a result of a boy’s grief over the death of his older brother. It is a daring but successful endeavor on the part of the author</span>
  <span id="freeText10751252605960657900" style="display:none"><br />I read this for Kimi's birthday tomorrow, Nov. 29! I'm posting it now because I might be too busy tomorrow. <b>HAPPY, HAPPY BIRTHDAY, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/17065991-kimi" rel="nofollow noopener">KIMI!</a> PUT A SMILE AS BIG AS YOUR HEART BECAUSE YOU DESERVE TO BE THE HAPPIEST ON YOUR SPECIAL DAY!</b> &lt;3 You can read her awesome review <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1007436230?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>.<br /><br /><b> Review </b><br /><br />This is an interesting read that deals with mental illness, more particularly schizophrenia as a result of a boy’s grief over the death of his older brother. It is a daring but successful endeavor on the part of the author to unravel the tangled world a person with schizophrenia lives in.<br /><br />It’s a devastating but eye-opening reading experience as Matthew relates in this unadulterated voice how a person like him copes with his kind of illness. We don’t read a lot of these books and this is why books like this deserve to be read and appreciated.<br /><br />The pacing however was a little slow and the plot tended to be monotonous and at times repetitive. The sporadic, garbled kind of writing has an intriguing quality to it especially during the first half of the story and it made perfect sense because of the condition of the narrator. But after more than 150 pages of said writing, the novelty began to wane and it started to become a bit irritating. It’s the kind a reader has to be very patient with in order to appreciate it. It’s the kind of read that you should be in the right mood in to appreciate it. Nonetheless, I wouldn’t contradict the blurb when it said <i>
  <b>“this is a brave and groundbreaking novel from one of the most exciting new voices in fiction.” </b>
</i><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10751252605960657900" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

It also seems fitting that I should let Matthew do most of the talking when it comes to telling you what this book is about.<br><br>Matthew has been raised by a mother who “is thin and pale, with cold hands. She has a broad chin that she is very self-conscious about. She sniffs the milk before she drinks it. She loves me. And she is mad.” And a father who “is tall and broad, and stoops a little. He wears a leather jacket because he used to ride a motorbike. He calls me mon ami. And he loves me.” He lived with a brother named “Simon. I think you’re going to like him. I really do. But in a couple of pages he’ll be dead. And he was never the same after that.”<br><br>Matthew was never quite the same after that, either. He’ll tell you that “you notice it when he isn’t there anymore. You notice so many of the places where he isn’t, and you hear so many of the things he doesn’t say. I do. I hear them all the time.”<br><br>Matthew will have to confront those demons of the past in order to come to terms with the reality of the present. Generally I find cover blurbs to be wholly inaccurate, but “rare and brilliant” is a very fitting description for <i>Where the Moon Isn’t</i>. Filer <b>really</b> knows how to get you into a character’s soul.<br></span>

<div id="review_644473007" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/644473007" />
    <a title="Hannah Green" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16651009-hannah-green"><img alt="Hannah Green" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1429526872p2/16651009.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/644473007?book_show_action=true">Jun 17, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hannah Green" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hannah Green" href="/user/show/16651009-hannah-green">Hannah Green</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16651009-hannah-green?shelf=2013-reads">2013-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16651009-hannah-green?shelf=twentyfirst-century">twentyfirst-century</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer644473007" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13689748244869243354">It seems that, by pure coincidence, I have stumbled into a number of books regarding mental illness, however, the depiction that this book utilises is purely unique. This book is quite simply unlike anything else I have ever read, that is without doubt or question. <br/><br/>The use of various fonts interspersed with simple drawings complement well the inconsistent thought process which Matt's thought process follows. Moreover, the subtle references to past events, without explaining full details, created</span>
  <span id="freeText13689748244869243354" style="display:none">It seems that, by pure coincidence, I have stumbled into a number of books regarding mental illness, however, the depiction that this book utilises is purely unique. This book is quite simply unlike anything else I have ever read, that is without doubt or question. <br /><br />The use of various fonts interspersed with simple drawings complement well the inconsistent thought process which Matt's thought process follows. Moreover, the subtle references to past events, without explaining full details, created momentum in a plot which could simply have been a procession of unrelated ideas. This book encompassed so many themes on death, grieving and mental health issues that it also feels like it lasted so much longer than it really did - though without dragging in the slightest.<br /><br />Moreover, the experience that Nathan Filer has gained as a mental health nurse is apparent through his irreverent treatment of the subject matter. He does not idealise the staff or the patients, both of them have good days and bad days and this was remarkably refreshing. I could not deny that I did not gain something from the text, but it was also pleasant to find that an author did not shove his or her ideology down my throat to the extent that the book merely appeared distasteful. Even better was that Filer managed to inject sharp bursts of humour which cut through what could otherwise be an oppressive narrative to entertain and make the work somehow more real.<br /><br />This book is difficult and it is also disturbing. However, it grabbed my attention and held it so that I read the work in a single day yet relished every word. It is beautifully constructed and I'm sure it will not only remain with me for a long time because of its subject matter, but also because of its original construction. Many have said that this book will go far, and I am certainly inclined to agree with them.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13689748244869243354" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_838715656" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/838715656" />
    <a title="Arlene" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7221235-arlene"><img alt="Arlene" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/838715656?book_show_action=true">Jan 29, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Arlene" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Arlene" href="/user/show/7221235-arlene">Arlene</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781250026989" href="/book/show/17286816-where-the-moon-isn-t">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer838715656" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7647567052262834253">It must be me since reviews of this book were overly positive but I honestly don't know why I took the time to finish reading this novel. I'm baffled by comments that this story could make anyone laugh and cry. It is certainly neither stunning nor a book that one would have a hard time putting down, and I would never recommend this book considering the wealth of options available to readers.<br/><br/>The only positive aspect of this novel is that it presents a very realistic glimpse of what mental illness</span>
  <span id="freeText7647567052262834253" style="display:none">It must be me since reviews of this book were overly positive but I honestly don't know why I took the time to finish reading this novel. I'm baffled by comments that this story could make anyone laugh and cry. It is certainly neither stunning nor a book that one would have a hard time putting down, and I would never recommend this book considering the wealth of options available to readers.<br /><br />The only positive aspect of this novel is that it presents a very realistic glimpse of what mental illness looks and feels like. The inner thoughts and perspectives of a young man afflicted with mental illness are viewed in comparison to ways treatment centers, care givers, and family members function to serve the needs of their customers and loved ones. For me, the focus on Matthew's hard edges detracted from deeper reflection on other characters. The underlying secret behind Matthew's illness was predictable but Filer attempted to attach some level of mystery to the disclosure by waiting until the end of the book to reveal what had happened early in Matthew's life. The effect was less than satisfying. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7647567052262834253" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_749260792" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/749260792" />
    <a title="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library"><img alt="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1350750103p2/4551536.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/749260792?book_show_action=true">Oct 25, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" href="/user/show/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library">Maja (The Nocturnal Library)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781250026989" href="/book/show/17286816-where-the-moon-isn-t">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=debut-author">debut-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=amazing-writing">amazing-writing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=contemporary-fiction">contemporary-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=review-copy">review-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=own-a-dtb">own-a-dtb</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=male-pov">male-pov</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=reviewed-in-2013">reviewed-in-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=literary-fiction">literary-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer749260792" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7986567555032199187"><b>4.5 stars</b><br/>Nathan Filer’s debut stunned me and left me speechless. It’s been a long time since I read something so beautifully written. <br/><br/>Where the Moon Isn’t is a story told by Matthew Homes, a mentally ill nineteen-year-old. It’s a metafictional novel, as Matthew constantly and intentionally exposes himself as the author and communicates openly with the readers. He provides excuses when he’s unable to explain something or offer further details. He makes constant remarks about his mental stability,</span>
  <span id="freeText7986567555032199187" style="display:none"><b>4.5 stars</b><br>Nathan Filer’s debut stunned me and left me speechless. It’s been a long time since I read something so beautifully written. <br><br>Where the Moon Isn’t is a story told by Matthew Homes, a mentally ill nineteen-year-old. It’s a metafictional novel, as Matthew constantly and intentionally exposes himself as the author and communicates openly with the readers. He provides excuses when he’s unable to explain something or offer further details. He makes constant remarks about his mental stability, and his reasons for writing the story.<br><br>Matthew’s problems started when he lost his older brother Simon. Simon was a child with special needs and Matt often resented him for being the center of their parents’ attention. But when Simon died in an accident partly caused by Matthew, he kept on living in Matthews head, a product of his guild and schizophrenia combined.<br><br>From the start, Matthew’s placement in the mental institution and his slightly odd storytelling hint at the possibility that he’s not the most reliable of narrators. It is almost impossible to discern which parts of his story are true, and which are the product of a damaged mind. Matthew is only nineteen, extremely vulnerable, and his thoughts are all over the place, jumping through space and time from one short chapter to the next. But still, it’s his unforgettable voice that holds this narrative together firmly and effortlessly.<br><br><b>
  <i>I’ll tell you what happened because it will be a good way to introduce my brother. His name’s Simon. I think you’re going to like him. I really do. But in a couple of pages he’ll be dead. And he was never the same after that.</i>
</b><br><br>As Matthews mental health deteriorates, his narration becomes less coherent, often making no sense whatsoever. His relationships with family and his only friend go downhill fast, because, as Matt himself keeps pointing out, schizophrenia is a selfish illness. There is a lot of resentment between Matt and his parents. His early teen years were rebellious, probably because the schizophrenia already affected his moods, and he made life difficult for everyone, himself included. Even though Matthew grows in this story, his mental illness isn’t taken lightly as something that can be fixed overnight. It is a constant, life-long struggle one needs to accept and make peace with.<br><br>Nathan Filer is a brilliant young author with so much to offer. His first novel is endearingly odd and in many ways spectacular. I simply can’t wait to see what he’ll come up with next.<br><br><a href="http://www.thenocturnallibrary.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380226536i/681142.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="7986567555032199187" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Amy | littledevonnook" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10559838-amy-littledevonnook"><img alt="Amy | littledevonnook" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596620580p2/10559838.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1153788187?book_show_action=true">Jan 03, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amy | littledevonnook" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amy | littledevonnook" href="/user/show/10559838-amy-littledevonnook">Amy | littledevonnook</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007491452" href="/book/show/20754586-the-shock-of-the-fall">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10559838-amy-littledevonnook?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10559838-amy-littledevonnook?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1153788187" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3942763419889891728">Such an engaging read, straight into my favourites for the year!<br/><br/>- This novel follows the story of a young man named Matthew. We are told of the tragic death of Matthew's brother during childhood and how he blames himself for its occurrence. As the reader we are unsure as to whether Matthew is actually guilty of the death of his brother or whether it was just a tragic accident. Nearer the end of the novel we discover the real story as to how his brother died. <br/><br/>- The other vital element to this nov</span>
  <span id="freeText3942763419889891728" style="display:none">Such an engaging read, straight into my favourites for the year!<br /><br />- This novel follows the story of a young man named Matthew. We are told of the tragic death of Matthew's brother during childhood and how he blames himself for its occurrence. As the reader we are unsure as to whether Matthew is actually guilty of the death of his brother or whether it was just a tragic accident. Nearer the end of the novel we discover the real story as to how his brother died. <br /><br />- The other vital element to this novel is that not only does Matthew blame himself, but he is also slowly descending into schizophrenia. We watch as his mental health suffers under the pressure of the self-inflicted guilt surrounding his brothers death. Seeing Matthew grow throughout the novel was touching.<br /><br />- For me, Matthews narrative voice was the best bit about this novel. I became really attached to him as a character and really wanted him to succeed in overcoming the struggles in his life. The flow of his words and the way they came off the page was fantastic and I became totally absorbed by his voice. If you like a book with a beautifully captivating protagonist - this may be the one for you!<br /><br />- Nathan Filer, being a mental health nurse has quite obviously had a lot of experience within this field and from the writing you can see how much he has fully immersed himself in the characters and relationships. If you have any interest in mental health or specifically schizophrenia this is a must read!<br /><br />- 5 out of 5 stars and I will definitely be picking up anything else from Filer in the future!</span>

<div id="review_569033547" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Diane S ☔" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4159922-diane-s"><img alt="Diane S ☔" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598402138p2/4159922.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/569033547?book_show_action=true">Mar 23, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Diane S ☔" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Diane S ☔" href="/user/show/4159922-diane-s">Diane S ☔</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781250026989" href="/book/show/17286816-where-the-moon-isn-t">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer569033547" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4290345192675138727">I have never read anything quite like this book before, it is a unique experience traveling along in the mindset of a mentally ill young man. I remember going to the theaters and seeing the movie "Beautiful Minds", I loved this movie, was completely blown away. That is how I felt at the end of this book. First time book for author Nathan Filer, and since he was a mental health nurse in previous years, he knew what he was writing about.<br/><br/>Matthew, our unreliable narrator, has a voice that is very re</span>
  <span id="freeText4290345192675138727" style="display:none">I have never read anything quite like this book before, it is a unique experience traveling along in the mindset of a mentally ill young man. I remember going to the theaters and seeing the movie "Beautiful Minds", I loved this movie, was completely blown away. That is how I felt at the end of this book. First time book for author Nathan Filer, and since he was a mental health nurse in previous years, he knew what he was writing about.<br /><br />Matthew, our unreliable narrator, has a voice that is very real and very innocent. After a tragedy in his family, from which he never really recovers, the trigger for his illness is set. We follow him as he tries to live in a life that is difficult and strange, for him things are never simple. His stays in a psychiatric wards and how his days are spent there, repeatedly going over the same things again and again, doing the same things , again and again. His courage and determination to get well, to write it all down so it could maybe make sense. Wanting to have a life, live on his own, the right to live in his own head if he wants too. Little victories, large set backs all poignantly rendered. It was impossible for me not to embrace this character, by books end we know almost everything about him and want everything to work out for him. <br /><br />In the beginning I wondered what was going on in this book but as the reader continues with the story , he is amply rewarded. More and more things are revealed as Matthews story goes back and forth. Wonderful first novel and look forward to many more.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4290345192675138727" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_870499408" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Dem" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2752994-dem"><img alt="Dem" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1552868566p2/2752994.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/870499408?book_show_action=true">Mar 03, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dem" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dem" href="/user/show/2752994-dem">Dem</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer870499408" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17421163259515440513">Nathan Filer's Debut Novel The Shock of The Fall is haunting and very real insight to death and mental illness.<br/><br/>I was recommended this novel and was assured it was a good audio book as I struggle with audio as opposed to reading and I have to say the narrator is excellent and he totally draws you into the character of Matthew to such an extinct that you feel it is actually Matthew narrating the story.<br/><br/>Matt Holmes is a 19 year old schizophrenic struggling within the mental health system who decides</span>
  <span id="freeText17421163259515440513" style="display:none">Nathan Filer's Debut Novel The Shock of The Fall is haunting and very real insight to death and mental illness.<br /><br />I was recommended this novel and was assured it was a good audio book as I struggle with audio as opposed to reading and I have to say the narrator is excellent and he totally draws you into the character of Matthew to such an extinct that you feel it is actually Matthew narrating the story.<br /><br />Matt Holmes is a 19 year old schizophrenic struggling within the mental health system who decides to put his thoughts to paper when his Nana buys him an old typewriter and hopes his scribbling and notes will be therapeutic and bring him some freedom.<br /><br /> <b>
  <i> I have an illness, a disease with the shape and sound of a snake. Whenever I learn something new it learns it too.......................My illness knows everything I know.</i>
</b>  <br /><br />The story is an unsettling and yet important one and really makes you think about the difficult subject of mental illness and the struggles of patients and families. I believe the author worked in this field himself and therefore had a good insight into the topic he choose to write about.<br /><br />It is by no means an uplifting story but it definitely is worth reading. It may not be everyone's cup of tea but I think if you have a look at the reviews and do choose to read it you will not be disappointed.<br /><br />This would make a good book club read as there is plenty of discussion in it. I loved the cover and the title of this book and will buy a copy as would like to have it to read another time.<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17421163259515440513" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_994818730" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/994818730" />
    <a title="Lotte" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25309949-lotte"><img alt="Lotte" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1408555448p2/25309949.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/994818730?book_show_action=true">Jul 13, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lotte" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lotte" href="/user/show/25309949-lotte">Lotte</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007491452" href="/book/show/20754586-the-shock-of-the-fall">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25309949-lotte?shelf=2015-read">2015-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25309949-lotte?shelf=ge-ya-contemporary">ge-ya-contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25309949-lotte?shelf=2015-priority">2015-priority</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25309949-lotte?shelf=t-diverse-reads">t-diverse-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25309949-lotte?shelf=t-mental-health">t-mental-health</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25309949-lotte?shelf=x-made-me-cry">x-made-me-cry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25309949-lotte?shelf=a-young-adult-fiction">a-young-adult-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25309949-lotte?shelf=2015-favourites">2015-favourites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer994818730" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17019889397100528294">I read the majority of this book within the last 24 hours. I just couldn’t stop reading and even neglected some of the stuff I should’ve been doing instead. Oops. But good books have the ability to make you forget everything around you, and <i>The Shock of the Fall</i> did just that. <br/><br/><blockquote>‘I’ll tell you what happened because it will be a good way to introduce my brother. His name’s Simon. I think you’re going to like him. I really do. But in a couple of pages he’ll be dead. And he was never the same after t</blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText17019889397100528294" style="display:none">I read the majority of this book within the last 24 hours. I just couldn’t stop reading and even neglected some of the stuff I should’ve been doing instead. Oops. But good books have the ability to make you forget everything around you, and <i>The Shock of the Fall</i> did just that. <br /><br /><blockquote>‘I’ll tell you what happened because it will be a good way to introduce my brother. His name’s Simon. I think you’re going to like him. I really do. But in a couple of pages he’ll be dead. And he was never the same after that.’<br />There are books you can’t stop reading, which keep you up all night. There are books which let us into the hidden parts of life and make them vividly real. There are books which, because of the sheer skill with which every word is chosen, linger in your mind for days. The Shock of the Fall is all of these books.<br />The Shock of the Fall is an extraordinary portrait of one man’s descent into mental illness. It is a brave and groundbreaking novel from one of the most exciting new voices in fiction.</blockquote><br /><br />My favorite aspect of this book was probably the style of narration and the fact that the book was a metafiction in some ways. The protagonist and narrator Matthew is writing down his own story in various places and over a longer timespan, while his life is still progressing. We learn about conflicts in the past and in the present day. He often interrupts his own narration, reflecting on what he already mentioned and sometimes even foreshadowing on what's going to happen later. I will say however, that I was very happy that I knew about this style of narration before going into this book, because it might’ve confused me at first. <br />I’m convinced that Matthew’s voice is the reason why the book had the same strange addicting quality that these kind of books often have for me (other examples include <i>It’s Kind of a Funny Story, We Have Always Lived in The Castle, Forgive Me Leonard Peacock</i> - wow, these are all some hefty titles! :D). Mentally unstable narrators who offer unique views of the world are so interesting to me, and I love getting inside of their head. You could really feel how Nathan Filer immersed himself into this character and this story, so I couldn’t help but completely immerse myself as well. There was also a short interview with the author in the back of my edition which offered some insight into his work process, which was really interesting!<br />Somehow, I was really happy about the fact hat there was no romantic interest in this book, even though it’s technically a YA book, and I rarely see YA books without some sort of romantic story line. However, sometimes it feels like a romance is just thrown into the story for good measure. This book completely worked without romance (even though I would still say that it's a book about love... just a different kind of love!) and I really appreciate that!<br />So, yeah. That's all I wanted to say for now. If this review has made you curious in any way, definitely give this book a try! It's worth your time.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17019889397100528294" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1097894849" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1097894849" />
    <a title="Maxine (Booklover Catlady)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22943325-maxine-booklover-catlady"><img alt="Maxine (Booklover Catlady)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601761303p2/22943325.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1097894849?book_show_action=true">Nov 04, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maxine (Booklover Catlady)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maxine (Booklover Catlady)" href="/user/show/22943325-maxine-booklover-catlady">Maxine (Booklover Catlady)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007491452" href="/book/show/20754586-the-shock-of-the-fall">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Everyone</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22943325-maxine-booklover-catlady?shelf=could-not-put-down">could-not-put-down</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1097894849" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7137304073548230119">One of my more unique reads this one, I was wary of the hype around it, but really enjoyed reading it. I love the way the book is written, for a debut novel it's quite exceptional, it's an emotion stirring book and thought provoking too. <br/><br/>It's essentially the story of a young man's descent into mental illness, from childhood events to trying to live as an independent adult and on to life in a mental health care facility. <br/><br/><b>What is spectacular about this book is how immersed in our main character yo</b></span>
  <span id="freeText7137304073548230119" style="display:none">One of my more unique reads this one, I was wary of the hype around it, but really enjoyed reading it. I love the way the book is written, for a debut novel it's quite exceptional, it's an emotion stirring book and thought provoking too. <br><br>It's essentially the story of a young man's descent into mental illness, from childhood events to trying to live as an independent adult and on to life in a mental health care facility. <br><br><b>What is spectacular about this book is how immersed in our main character you get, he is telling the story of his life, his feelings, thoughts, his mental illness, it's a bit like sitting in the room with someone, listening avidly to their life story. And feeling things along the way.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1415266105ra/11760818.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The book cleverly gives you snippets of a story, then later on you get more of that story to give you the fuller picture, so there is a lot of a-ha moments, at least there was for me. I found it sad in parts, I really felt for his struggle against the illness that has hold of him, his moving between lucidity and delusion. Epically done. <br><br><b>Is it worth all the hype and a must read book? I think so. It's just different from almost all the books I have read this year. I found it easy to read, interesting, thought provoking and powerful with it's message sent. 4 stars from me. I really liked this one.</b></span>

<div id="review_1976268062" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1976268062" />
    <a title="GTF" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/66513638-gtf"><img alt="GTF" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594722618p2/66513638.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1976268062?book_show_action=true">May 13, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="GTF" class="user" itemprop="url" name="GTF" href="/user/show/66513638-gtf">GTF</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1976268062" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12719656913448927299">Many parts of "The Shock of the Fall" that aim to evoke sentimentality and sorrow, fall a little flat. The narration is very yappy, but that being said there are some nice quotes and occasional tenderness throughout the book. <br/> <br/>The plot was often gearing towards how Simon died, which really could have been told from the very beginning seen as the story was told from the perspective of Matthew (who was a witness) but instead it wasn't revealed till the very end. I acknowledge that it is a traumati</span>
  <span id="freeText12719656913448927299" style="display:none">Many parts of "The Shock of the Fall" that aim to evoke sentimentality and sorrow, fall a little flat. The narration is very yappy, but that being said there are some nice quotes and occasional tenderness throughout the book. <br /> <br />The plot was often gearing towards how Simon died, which really could have been told from the very beginning seen as the story was told from the perspective of Matthew (who was a witness) but instead it wasn't revealed till the very end. I acknowledge that it is a traumatic memory for Matthew but it didn't make much sense for him to wait so long to tell the reader given that Simon was one of the main subject matters of the book, and also because he was undergoing treatment for a large part of the story which involved counselling which would usually involve confronting traumatic memories. The entire memory of the death incident should have floated through Matthew's head at least once at an earlier stage in the story. When a book is being told from the perspective of a character, the reader is inside the character's head and therefore there are no secrets. But maybe I am only complaining about this as I found the death scene anti-climatic and not very surprising or memorable. <br /><br />Another issue with the character of Matthew, is that Matthew is a diagnosed schizophrenic but does not consistently exhibit the disorder. He does act strange on occasion but overall his language is coherent and his thought patterns are not that disrupted. Come to think of it, I don't think that a story could be told from the perspective of a schizophrenic as it would be very confusing and unintentionally erratic and I say this not with the intention of trivializing schizophrenia but instead highlighting how tragic a condition it really is, as it mentally separates sufferers of the disorder from the real world and sections them into a darker and isolating world due to erosion of cognitive functions. I think that the story would have been better told from the perspective of Simon's mother or else a third person narrative with Matthew still being a main character.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12719656913448927299" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_582257339" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/582257339" />
    <a title="Teresa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/402584-teresa"><img alt="Teresa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600814344p2/402584.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/582257339?book_show_action=true">Apr 05, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Teresa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Teresa" href="/user/show/402584-teresa">Teresa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer582257339" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3515174805269885766">Nathan Filer is a registered mental health nurse as well as a performance poet and his real-life experience is evident in this, his debut novel. The story is narrated by Matthew, a nineteen year old schizophrenic who recalls the sudden, tragic death of his older brother, Simon – a death which he believes he caused.<br/><br/>The use of mixed formats, different fonts interspersed with occasional line drawings cleverly mirrors the ebb and flow of Matthew’s mental illness. Likewise, the narrative flits betwee</span>
  <span id="freeText3515174805269885766" style="display:none">Nathan Filer is a registered mental health nurse as well as a performance poet and his real-life experience is evident in this, his debut novel. The story is narrated by Matthew, a nineteen year old schizophrenic who recalls the sudden, tragic death of his older brother, Simon – a death which he believes he caused.<br /><br />The use of mixed formats, different fonts interspersed with occasional line drawings cleverly mirrors the ebb and flow of Matthew’s mental illness. Likewise, the narrative flits between different stages in his life, before Simon’s death, after Simon’s death, during hospital stays, independent living. This is an extremely honest account of one man’s journey through mental illness but there is also humour and great insight from Matthew as he sees how his brother’s death tore his family apart and left them adrift.<br /><br />The characters are living, breathing creations, with their own foibles and imperfections. You see the heartache of Matthew’s parents who, having lost one son, feel they are losing their only remaining child. His Mum, is at her wits end, making lots of noise whilst Dad retreats into silence. His grandmother, the wonderful Nanny Noo, accepts Matthew as he is, visiting him at his flat every other Thursday, never passing judgement.<br /><br /> "If it wasn’t for Nanny Noo I wouldn’t give a shit, but when somebody cares for you as much as she does, I know it’s not nice to make them worry."<br /><br />This is a beautifully written, moving story – the beauty is in the everyday detail of Matthew’s life – from the fleeting memories of a holiday in France to the stultifying routine of an acute psychiatric ward – eat, sleep, smoke… It’s a novel which will stay with me when others have disappeared into the ether – you won’t forget Matthew in a hurry and you cannot fail to wish him well….or just to keep his head above water…</span>
  <a data-text-id="3515174805269885766" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_836342618" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/836342618" />
    <a title="Debumere" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7019056-debumere"><img alt="Debumere" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1458595399p2/7019056.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/836342618?book_show_action=true">Jan 27, 2014</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer15253455007186523820"><blockquote>We are selfish my illness and I. We think only of ourselves. We shape the world around us into messages, into secret whispers spoken only for us.</blockquote><br/>3.5 stars. This was upsetting, but very insightful. To describe the descent into schizophrenia in such a vivid and moving way, you must have some experience with this illness in real life. So it made perfect sense when I read that the author has been a registered mental health nurse, working in psychiatric wards, for more than a decade.<br/><br/>I think what I li</span>
  <span id="freeText15253455007186523820" style="display:none"><blockquote>We are selfish my illness and I. We think only of ourselves. We shape the world around us into messages, into secret whispers spoken only for us.</blockquote><br />3.5 stars. This was upsetting, but very insightful. To describe the descent into schizophrenia in such a vivid and moving way, you must have some experience with this illness in real life. So it made perfect sense when I read that the author has been a registered mental health nurse, working in psychiatric wards, for more than a decade.<br /><br />I think what I liked most about the book, is how Nathan Filer played with time. The story keeps jumping around in time, and quite a few times I wasn't sure where we were. This is what it must be like for Mat all the time - <i>Time falls through my fingers.</i> You can also feel the incredible sadness that surrounds the whole family after Simon died, and see how everyone tries to cope with the situation. Matthew is one of the most honest characters I've ever met, but that's possibly because his reality is not as fixed as most other people.<br />Also, I loved the cover.<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
